            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
        
        
        
        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The switch-hitting utility man, taken from the Nationals in the Rule 5 Draft, ended up getting more playing time than his limited skill set warranted. The career .263/.315/.368 minor league batter hit just .198/.258/.282 in 234 major league plate appearances. He posted a lower OBP than Kyle Kendrick, and was outslugged by Cliff Lee. Martinez qualifies in most leagues at second base, shortstop, third base and the outfield, and he could be given more than he can handle again in 2012 if Philly doesn’t add a more accomplished reserve infielder. If he’s on your roster, however, I can only assume you’re a masochist or Mama Martinez. (David Golebiewski)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Martinez aspires to be Wilson Valdez. Do I really need to say any more than that?</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Martinez was one of the worst hitters in the league last year and his pedigree offers little reason to expect significant improvement. (Jack Moore)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Multiple positions are always sexy in fantasy baseball, but Martinez is a 31-year-old utilityman with a career .187/.234/.261 slash who has had mixed hitting results in Triple-A. If he contributes meaningfully to any fantasy team in 2014, it might be the feel-good story of the season. (<a href="https://twitter.com/BradleyWoodrum">@BradleyWoodrum</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>There are almost definitely better utilityman options on the waiver wire. Martinez may be somewhat useful to a real team, but there's almost no chance his hitting and limited plate appearances will provide value in the fantasy sphere.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>In his major league career, Martinez has played all three outfield positions, second, third, and shortstop. That is valuable to a big league club. And if he got a chance to reacquire all that eligibility in fantasy, that would have theoretical value. But he's also a 33-year-old whose career slugging percentage would be a bad on-based percentage (and whose OBP would be a good, but far from great, batting average). He doesn't have power, he doesn't steal bases, he doesn't play often, and he doesn't really hit. I believe this is what's called a ringing endorsement! (Chad Young)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Martinez is a useful utility player for a team's 40-man, offering depth at almost any position. But he can't hit and has no place in fantasy.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Martinez is 34 years old, and he's a career .197/.241/.266 hitter in 578 major league plate appearances. He can't get on base, doesn't hit for power or steal bases, etc. He's old and wasn't good to begin with. (Scott Strandberg)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Martinez will not be relevant in any fantasy format in 2017.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
